A fire broke out at Longgenji Flower Clothing Factory, No. 270 Funing Road, Yangshupu, at 7:40 yesterday morning. The Yangshupu Fire Brigade drove to the scene to put out the fire, and it was quickly extinguished.

Mr. Zhang has a wide circle of friends throughout his life, and there must be a grand occasion with many visitors at that time.

Local Court Continues Hearing of the Baoshan Road Massacre Case

Yesterday, statements were still taken from various individuals

The plaintiff does not pursue the public prosecution

Regarding the case of the Fifth District Police Station of the Public Security Bureau killing civilians on Baoshan Road, the local court held another hearing yesterday morning. At 10:00 a.m., the courtroom was already packed with spectators, and police chief Xu Jinqing, police officers Chen Xihui, Chen Junfang, etc., supervised the bailiffs to maintain order section by section. At 10:30 a.m., presiding judge Qian Chengjun, along with judges Zhao Yongzhou and Shen Youxi, prosecutor Yang Wenjun, and clerk Yu Bi, arrived at the first courtroom to begin the hearing. The defendants' lawyers were Sha Xunyi, Zhu Shaowen, Qu (acting for Zhang Yaozeng), Tao Jiachun, etc. The attorney for the victims, Wang Hexing, Qian Shusheng, appeared in court and stated that the private prosecution part had been compensated by the municipal government and requested withdrawal. As for the public prosecution part, there was no need to pursue it, and requested the court to handle it accordingly. At this point, the judge questioned the victim.

Zhang Baolin testified, age twenty-two, from Changzhou, and is a carpenter. (Asked) When were you at the entrance of the Fifth District? (Answered) I forgot the date, around 8 p.m. (Asked) Who were you with? (Answered) I was going home to sleep alone. (Asked) What did you see? (Answered) I don't know, because there were so many people, I tried to squeeze through, but unexpectedly, they started shooting. (Asked) When you squeezed, were you facing the Fifth District? (Answered) My face was facing east. (Asked) Where did the bullet enter? (Answered) It entered my lower left back and exited on the right side. (Asked) Was it from behind? (Answered) Yes. (Asked) Facing east, were you facing the district? (Answered) I was going back. (Asked) Which direction faces the district? (Answered) The left. (Asked) How was the bullet removed after being shot? (Answered) I first went to Jisheng Hospital, and they said the bullet had already exited. I didn't believe it, so I went to the Labor Hospital and had an X-ray taken. They also said the bullet had exited. (Asked) Has the injury fully healed now? (Answered) It has healed, but I can't work. (Asked) Who fired the gun? (Answered) I only know that it was fired from the entrance of the Fifth District. Two people who were injured in the hospital told me. (Asked) What are their names? (Answered) I don't know. At this point, the judge questioned the witness.

Feng Xiancheng testified, age twenty-nine, from Gaoyou, and is a standing committee member of the Sixth District Party Headquarters. The judge ordered him to first provide a written statement, then (Asked) Do you know You Bolu? (Answered) I know him through official business dealings. (Asked) When did you go to the district? (Answered) I went once at 6 p.m. on October 1st, then returned. I went again at 7:45 p.m. (Asked) What was the first time for? (Answered) There was a conflict between the police and soldiers over posting slogans. We were in a meeting when someone reported that many people were surrounding the police station. For the sake of security, I went with Yang Youren and Wen Renan. I saw district member Guo Chenggai said that the district chief was not there, and the police officers had closed the station. They would handle it when the district chief arrived. I immediately told the soldiers, who were very satisfied. I then told the soldiers, "The people are here for you, you should report to the people so they know the reason." The soldiers stood on a high place and explained, and the people were also satisfied and dispersed. (Asked) What were the soldiers called? (Answered) Dong Guokai, Fu Jishan, and I forgot one name. Fu Jishan stood up and spoke. (Asked) How many people were there at that time? (Answered) More than 500 people. (Asked) Did they all disperse? (Answered) Part of them dispersed, and part of them seemed to disperse but didn't. A part of them came to the District Party Headquarters, and Yang Youren reported that the matter was over. (Asked) How did the accident happen again? (Answered) Later, someone came to report that the police station in the district was beating the people with batons. I said that the explanation was very satisfactory at the time, how could they not disperse? He said there were other reasons. At 3 o'clock today, several Japanese people came and went out with the district chief. The district chief must have been influenced by the Japanese, so he prohibited posting slogans. Yang Youren and I went again. (Asked) How many people were in front of the district? (Answered) More than a thousand people, all on both sides of the road. They did not obstruct the Public Security Bureau's gate, nor did they obstruct traffic. But after we went in, the crowd rushed in and leveled the bureau's gate. (Asked) Did the people go in? (Answered) At that time, I was talking to the district chief. (Asked) What were the people saying? (Answered) Very noisy. (Asked) How did the shooting start? (Answered) I went up and told District Chief You to explain it, so You stood on a bench and gave a speech to the people, but the people didn't seem to hear and were still cursing. (Asked) What did he explain? (Answered) He said that the Japanese came today to inquire about the detained Japanese goods. Later, we also explained, but the people still did not disperse. Unexpectedly, a bus came and wanted to drive, but I don't know how the people beat the bus driver. The police went to rescue the bus driver. I immediately ordered the tea room of the District Party Headquarters to quickly call the artillery team at the railway station to explain, because they caused the trouble. Later, I took a hat and was pushed into a hardware store by the people. I heard gunshots, I don't know where they came from. (Asked) You must know if anyone was killed. (Answered) I was in the middle of the dead people. (Asked) How far away? (Answered) One person was near the Fifth District gate, about one zhang away. There was also one farther away. (Asked) How many gunshots did you hear? (Answered) The first time was continuous, seven or eight shots. The second time, there were one or two shots. At this point, the judge asked.

Guo Chenggai testified, age thirty-seven, from Sichuan, and is a district member of the Fifth District. (Asked) On October 1st, when did You Bolu come to the district? (Answered) A little after 7 o'clock. (Asked) How many people were in front of the district? (Answered) Not many at 6 o'clock, but more at 8 o'clock. They were shouting "Down with District Chief You" and slogans about seizing guns. (Asked) What time was this? (Answered) A little after 8 o'clock. (Asked) Where were you? (Answered) In front of the detention center. The district chief and patrol officer were mostly outside. (Asked) Did a bus pass by? (Answered) Yes, the driver was beaten and shouted for help. The police went to see, and they wanted to seize the gun. Later, I heard gunshots. (Asked) Was it fired by the police? (Answered) Yes, but it was fired into the sky. (Asked) What was the cause of the incident? (Answered) Around 6 o'clock, police officer Guo Wenhan stopped the soldiers from posting slogans on the police kiosk, and a verbal dispute arose. The soldiers put paste on the police officer's body, and the police officer retaliated by hitting his wrist with a stick, which led to the conflict. (Asked) What other reasons were there? (Answered) The skin was detained by the anti-Japanese association. The Japanese within the jurisdiction of the Fifth District came to the Public Security Bureau to negotiate because there was no news. This was bought by the Japanese from the Chinese and should be returned. The Public Security Bureau sent someone to the Fifth District. (Asked) Was You Bochuo in the district at that time? (Answered) Yes, he was in the district. (Asked) Was You there when the slogans were posted? (Answered) No, he was not there. (Asked) After the crowd dispersed, how did they gather again? (Answered) I don't know. (Asked) Did You Bolu order the shooting? (Answered) I don't know because I was inside, but I think even without the district chief's order, the police officers were acting in self-defense by firing two shots into the air, and it was appropriate. At this point, the judge (asked).

Wu Decai testified, age twenty-three, from Zhenjiang, and is a bus driver. The judge ordered him to provide a written statement first, then (Asked) What time did you drive to the entrance of the Fifth District on October 1st? (Answered) I left Baoshan Road at 8:15 and arrived in front of the district at 8:20 something. (Asked) What happened after arriving in front of the district? (Answered) There were so many people, I honked the horn, and they blocked the front of the district and didn't allow me to drive. They beat the bus. I said that we are all Chinese, not Japanese. They dragged me down and beat me until I passed out. A chief inspector, Shi Tifen, and a police officer rescued me. (Asked) What did the people do later? (Answered) They all rushed to the entrance of the Fifth District. (Asked) What slogans did you hear them shout? (Answered) Down with the Fifth District. (Asked) Did you hear gunshots? (Answered) I only heard robbing, I don't know what they were robbing. (Asked) You must have heard the shooting. (Answered) I heard it, but I don't know where it came from. (Asked) How many shots were fired? (Answered) More than a dozen shots. (Asked) You passed out at that time, how did you hear it? (Answered) I had woken up. (Asked) Did you see who fired the gun? (Answered) I was lying on the ground and didn't see. (Asked) What were you beaten with? (Answered) Fists. At this point, the judge (asked).

Shi Tifen testified, age twenty-three, from Ningbo, and works as a chief inspector at the bus company. The judge ordered him to provide a written statement first, then (Asked) Do you know You Bolu? (Answered) I don't know him. (Asked) What did you do at the bureau on October 1st? (Answered) That day, I was attending a meeting at the District Party Headquarters, and someone came to report. (Asked) What time did you go to the district? (Answered) Around 7 o'clock. At that time, the people were making a fuss. Comrade Feng told the district chief to talk it over. (Asked) What was the situation in front of the Fifth District? (Answered) There were about two thousand people, saying "Beat You Bolu." After explaining on the bench, the people left and then came back and beat my driver to the ground. I went to drag the driver up and shouted for help. They knocked off my glasses. Later, the police came and rescued us. (Asked) Did the district chief order the shooting? (Answered) Yes. (Asked) What happened after the shooting? (Answered) The people left. (Asked) How did the shooting happen? (Answered) I saw shots fired into the sky. At this point, (asked).

When You Bolu fired the gun, what was the situation? (Answered) Because they rushed in, I fired shots into the sky to scare them. (Asked) Who did you tell the police? (Answered) Liu Weicheng. (Asked) Did other police officers fire after Liu fired? (Answered) They also followed suit and fired. After the people retreated, I immediately forbade them to shoot. I saw two dead people on the road, and there were also gunshots outside. I wanted to investigate whether they were pistol wounds or Mauser wounds, and didn't want them to kill people and harm me. At this point, (asked).

How many shots did Liu Weicheng fire? (Answered) Two shots fired into the sky. (Asked) Were there gunshots outside? (Answered) There were already gunshots outside. (Asked) How did You Bolu teach you to shoot? (Answered) Fire into the sky. The brothers followed suit and fired. At this point, (asked).

Lin Qingxiang fired how many shots (Answered) Two shots, fired into the sky, following the district chief's orders, and (asked).

Wu Maolin (Answered) Fired one shot. Liu Weicheng fired two shots first, and the people still rushed in, so we two fired. It was ordered by the district chief, otherwise we wouldn't dare. The rest is the same, and (asked).

Qiao Xuechang testified, fired two shots, the rest of the testimony is the same, and asked. Wu Zhanyou testified, fired one shot, the rest of the testimony is the same. At this point, the judge announced that there was still a need to summon witnesses, and no debate would be held. The hearing would be held again later. You's lawyer requested bail, but the judge did not allow it and ordered him to be remanded in custody.

The Second District Public Security Bureau Cracks Down on a Large Number of Thieves

A pistol hidden in a hollow wooden stool

Eight people arrested in a search

Since taking office, Ling Xichao, the district chief of the Second District Public Security Bureau, has paid great attention to robbery cases occurring within the district, so he strictly ordered Cao Junda, the leader of the district's investigation team, to arrest the perpetrators. It is now known that on the 3rd of this month, informant Chen Wentong reported that there were bandits hiding in house number 347 at the intersection of Luban Road and Xietu Road, etc. He immediately reported to leader Cao Junda, who reported to District Chief Ling and secretly dispatched investigators Chen Wentong, Wang Tingge, Shen Jinchu, Gao Lanchun, Zhu Jinxiu, etc., armed to investigate the area. They arrested the thieves Sun Xuqing, Li Pinwan, Fan Sanfu, and the suspects Qiu Mingcai, Ji A'er, Wang Dingfu, Ji Xianfa, Zhao Baocheng, and eight others. They also found a Brownlin pistol with serial number 35439 containing six bullets under Sun's pillow, as well as a hollow wooden stool used to hide the pistol, and brought them all back to the district office. According to Li Pinwan's confession, there was another pistol hidden in Fan Sanfu's house at Gu's residence on Tao Erfeisi Road in the French Concession. Therefore, leader Cao sent a detective to accompany the suspect to the French Concession and work with Chinese and Western detectives from the Songshan Road Police Station to drive to the above address. They found a Brownlin pistol with serial number 1505 containing seven bullets and brought it back to the district. After further interrogation of Sun Xuqing, he confessed that there was also an accomplice, Chang Wangzi, whose real name was Zhang Zaixin, living in the second room of the Yangshupu Water Plant. The detectives then took Sun to the Public Concession and cooperated with the Yangshupu Police Station to arrest Zhang Zaixin, but he was not found. Only two Brownlin pistols with serial numbers 32650 and 29248 were found in the drawer of the house and brought back to the district. District Chief Ling interrogated them one by one, and they confessed to the robbery of a certain case in South Shanghai and a certain village in Wuxi, etc. After a brief interrogation by District Chief Ling, he prepared a document and sent it to the Third Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for a secret investigation. The names, ages, and addresses of the thieves and suspects are listed below: Sun Xuqing, age 29, from Haimen, currently residing at house number 347 at the intersection of Luban Road and Xietu Road; Li Pinwan, age 32, from Tongzhou, with no fixed address; Fan Sanfu, age 41, from Tongzhou, residing at Gu's residence on Tao Erfeisi Road in the French Concession; suspect Ji A'er, age 30, from Haimen, residing in Yuanchang Lane, Hualong Road; Wang Dingfu, age 33, from Tongzhou, residing at house number 9, Shunxing Lane, Luban Road; Ji Xianfa, age 46, from Haimen, with no address; Qiu Mingcai, age 28, from Tongzhou, residing at house number 10, Saporose Road in the French Concession; Zhao Baocheng, age 43, from Tongzhou, residing at house number 347 at the intersection of Xietu Road.

Overseas Chinese Enthusiastically Donate for Disaster Relief

During this domestic flood, overseas Chinese from all over the world are particularly enthusiastic about relief efforts. In addition to remittances and clothing being sent one after another, Mr. Hu Wenhu of Singapore also sent many boxes of Wan Jin Oil to the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Association for distribution. Recently, the association also received 24,000 cans of special jackfruit from the Hawaii Boro Company in Honolulu, USA, instructing them to convert the price into grain and distribute it to the flood-stricken areas. The Wing On Company on Nanjing Road in this city has also volunteered to sell it on consignment, jointly contributing to the good cause. It is said that the products are of good quality and low price. Large cans are sold at a reduced price of two cans per dollar, and medium cans are sold at three cans per dollar, which is only half the price of those sold on the market. Many Westerners are buying them. Not only can they enjoy delicious food, but they can also help disaster victims, which is truly a win-win situation.

The Deadline for Accepting Disaster Victims is Today

The number of people already sheltered is over 10,000

Those who come later will not be sent away or provided for

The Shanghai Disaster Relief Committee held its sixth regular meeting at 6 p.m. yesterday. Chairman of the committee Qu Wenliu, Huang Hanzhi, Wang Binyan, Hu Hongji (represented by Jiang Shicheng), Ma Shaoping, Gu Junyang, Xu Shiying, Xu Feng, Cheng Yiqing (represented by Wang Shaoyun), Chen Liangyu, Wang Yiting, and Zhu Qiluo, Chairman Xu Jingren discussed, (1) Within the last two weeks, more than 300 disaster victims have been sent away twice, but the number of shelters has increased by 2,000 people. The current total number of shelters is already over 10,000, and it will continue to increase. How should this be handled? The public decided that the deadline will be tomorrow (that is, today), and no more will be accepted. No sending away, no providing for, and merging shelters as much as possible. (2) Jiang Zhejun, the deputy director of the management group, resigned due to illness, and Xu Yun was hired to succeed him, specializing in management affairs. Another deputy director was added, and Ma Shaoping was hired to specialize in supply affairs. Each person is responsible for their own responsibilities and thoroughly reorganizes the public decision and passed. (3) The association received a telegram from Ma Qing of Gaoyou, etc., requesting that disaster victims continue to be sheltered and that those who have no home should be temporarily delayed from returning to their original homes. The public decided to handle the first case together. (4) After the association took over the staff of the shelter, except for some changes in the health group, the management group part was terminated within the time limit originally agreed upon by the association, so everything remains as it was. Now that there are more shelters, the income and expenditure are huge. It is planned to add regulations to the salaries and wages of all management group members and servants in order to prepare a budget. The two deputy directors, Xu and Ma, are responsible for thoroughly implementing the public decision. The budget table was passed. (5) A report on income and expenditure within two weeks (omitted).

The Christian Deng Hui, Dong Jingan, and others organized a flood relief association and received approximately 15,000 yuan in donations. Starvation Deaths of Disaster Victims on the Jianghua Ship

The impact of the crew's work stoppage

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's crew members' request for double pay at the end of the year led to a work stoppage, which has lasted for four days. All ships are docked at the pier. It is known that the company's Yangtze River Jianghua ship was originally scheduled to be boarded free of charge by the company on the 7th to go to the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. The city's Disaster Relief Committee had 86 disaster victims from Hubei who were transported to Jiujiang, Mianyang, and other places to return to their hometowns. On the evening of the 7th, they were transported and boarded the Jianghua ship, which was approved by the company for free passage. Each adult was given 2 yuan for food, and each child was given 1 yuan for food, which was handed over to the ship's purser for safekeeping to be used for food. Unexpectedly, the ship stopped sailing on that day due to the crew's demand for wages, causing the disaster victims in the lower艙 to not only have no hope of returning to their hometowns, but also had nothing to eat. As of yesterday, they had been starving for three days and were on the verge of death. Among them, an old woman named Yang Xu, age 58, could not bear the hunger and collapsed in the cabin at 3 p.m. yesterday and died. After being discovered by someone, it was reported to the court for inspection and collection of the body. At the same time, the Disaster Relief Committee received the news and sent staff to the Jianghua ship's pier last night to distribute food to the disaster victims.

Cancellation of Monthly Bonuses at Two Japanese Factories Causes Disputes

The old silk factory has been resolved

The Rihua Yarn Factory has no solution yet

Part of the workers at the Dongyang Silk Factory on Houmalu Road in Caojiadu, West Shanghai, and all the workers at the Rihua Yarn Factory on Robert Seng Road went on strike yesterday morning because the factory suddenly canceled their monthly bonuses. The details of the incident are recorded below.

Old Silk Factory

Dongyang on Houmalu Road in Caojiadu

The old silk factory also has a new factory in Singapore Road. There are a total of eight or nine hundred workers. The business has been developing and profitable in recent years. As a general rule, the factory provides a monthly bonus of eight工 for each worker out of consideration and encouragement. At the end of each month, it is issued by name (all Japanese factories have this monthly bonus, but there are slight differences in the amount). Recently, various Japanese factories have suffered losses due to the impact of boycotts. Maintaining operations has been difficult to support. After repeated meetings by the Japanese factories, it was decided to cancel the monthly bonus across the board from last month to reduce expenses. After the factory announced the cancellation, all the workers, because the cost of living is increasing day by day and they work hard for a month, rely on this monthly bonus to make up for the shortfall. They repeatedly requested the factory to issue it, but it was ineffective. Therefore, a part of the factory's workers, about one hundred and dozens of people, went on strike after arriving at the factory yesterday morning. Ren, the district chief of the Sixth District Police Station, immediately led Inspector Xu to the factory after receiving the report. After comforting the workers and mediating with the Japanese factory, the factory agreed in the afternoon to give half the bonus each month, that is, each person gets four 工 each month. The workers were grateful for District Chief Ren's sincere mediation, so a peaceful resolution was reached. All the workers also went to work and returned to normal.

Rihua Yarn Factory

The factory has always given a monthly bonus of only four 工 to each worker. Now that the factory has announced the cancellation, all the workers, about two thousand people, are very panicked. They also went on strike yesterday morning, demanding that the factory issue the bonus as before. After receiving the report, District Chief Ren of the Sixth District immediately ordered Inspector Gu of the First Branch to lead the police to maintain order. On one hand, he personally led Inspector Xu to the factory to persuade and mediate with the factory and all the workers. Because the workers are struggling to make a living, their attitude is very firm, and the factory has suffered too much loss due to the boycott, so there is still no resolution by the evening.

The Rihua Factory Storm is Difficult to Resolve

More than 300 female workers in the cloth machine room of the Pudong Rihua Yarn Factory went on strike at the end of last year because they refused to accept the factory's deduction of wages. After several mediations by the authorities, the two sides became extreme and are about to break up. The workers in each room also provided financial assistance and urged the workers in that room to adhere to the original agreement and not to make any more concessions, in order to fall for the Japanese traitors' tricks. The female workers also took a firm attitude and went to work in various Chinese yarn factories in Puxi in batches for days to persevere. The Rihua branch office of the Fifth District Textile Workers' Union issued a letter to all workers in the city yesterday, appealing for assistance. The wording is omitted.

The Jing'an Temple Monk May Settle the Lawsuit

The abbot of Jing'an Temple, Zhiwen, was ill and entrusted his younger brother, Zhifa, to act as the abbot. Unexpectedly, Zhiwen recovered from his illness and returned to the temple, but Zhiba refused to move out, resulting in a lawsuit in court, which has not been resolved. It is now heard that both parties have repented, believing that monks should have no worldly possessions and should not be involved in endless lawsuits. Therefore, they have each asked powerful people to mediate a reconciliation.

A Woman Carries More Than 10,000 Red Pills

Six months of imprisonment...60 yuan fine

Inspector Yao Jialin of the China Patrol learned that someone was selling red pills for profit at house number 189, Burton Road, so the day before yesterday, he secretly went to search the place with Chinese and Western police. They saw a Jiangxi woman, Fu Jin, holding two white cloth bags, preparing to go out to sell them. They were immediately stopped and searched. The bags were filled with red pills, with a total of more than 10,000 pills. They also found 80 yuan in paper money in her pocket, as well as an account book and a notebook, all of which recorded the sales of red pills. They were all brought into the Hongkou Police Station. The police chief ordered her to be transferred to the women's detention center for temporary detention. Yesterday morning, she was sent to the First Special Court, Court One. After Judge Xiao interrogated Fu Jin, he immediately sentenced her to six months of imprisonment and a fine of 60 yuan. If she could not pay the fine, she would be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. The paper money, notebook, and red pills were confiscated.

Pawnbroking an Niece into Prostitution

Wang Daheng, a resident of Zhenjiang living at No. 204 North Jiangxi Road in Shanghai, had a niece named Zhang Fengying, aged sixteen. When she was seven, her mother, Zhang Wang, entrusted her to Wang's care. Unexpectedly, Wang colluded with a Suzhou woman, Sun Jiang, and on September 15th of last year, sold Zhang Fengying to a woman surnamed Zhang at No. 275 Yanqing Lane, Xiamen Road, to become a private prostitute. They received 350 silver dollars from the transaction. The case was discovered by the girl's mother, Zhang Wang, who came to Shanghai from Zhenjiang some days ago and hired a lawyer to report the matter to the Hongkou Police Station. Detective Bao Shuji was dispatched to arrest Wang Daheng and Sun Jiang one after another, and the girl Zhang Fengying was rescued. All were handed over to the First Special District Court. Zhang Wang accused Wang Daheng, as Fengying's maternal uncle, of improperly selling his niece into prostitution and demanded severe punishment. Wang Daheng brazenly claimed that his niece Fengying had volunteered for such a life of physical labor and that the money obtained would be used to prepare her fiancé's betrothal gifts. Zhang Fengying was ordered to be returned to her mother to return to her hometown, and the two defendants were detained pending a scheduled sentencing. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xieqiao rendered the verdict in the First Higher Court, sentencing Wang Daheng to six months of imprisonment and Sun Jiang to three months of imprisonment. The number of days of detention prior to the final judgment will be used to offset the imprisonment at a rate of two days offsetting one day.

A Monstrosity in Pudong

Cat-headed, Green-eyed Creature Thrown to Death After Birth

A local man named Jiang, who lives near Shenjia Lane in Pudong and makes a living by rowing boats, married a woman surnamed Mou. They already have two sons. Around February last year, the wife became pregnant. Recently, her belly became very large, and on the night before last, she gave birth to a monster. It had a large head with a pointed snout that already had teeth, resembling a cat. The ears pointed upwards, almost identical to cat ears. The eyes were green, and the hands and feet were extremely small. The chest and abdomen were similar to a human's body. Jiang was shocked upon seeing it and gathered his neighbors to observe. None of them knew what it was. Jiang then threw the monster to the ground, killing it. That night, he hung it on a roadside fence to show the public and prevent it from being reincarnated. The superstition of ignorant commoners is evident. Yesterday morning, a man nicknamed "He Yun the Blind" saw it and was amazed. He immediately took it down to the rural area east of Yangjing Temple and shouted, attracting a crowd of farmers. He charged each person two copper coins for a look, earning six or seven hundred copper coins in a short time. Later, fearing being caught by the police and suffering undeserved disaster, he threw it into a toilet and left. According to the report, this monster was likely due to a physiological anomaly.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: The weather will be clear and cold. There is fog in several places along the Yangtze River and along the coast here. There will be occasional seasonal winds over the Yellow Sea and East China Sea, from the northwest and northeast. Unstable wind and rain in northern Shandong due to a low-pressure system passing through Mongolia and moving towards the southeast-east. Also, the local temperature in the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday was a maximum of 45.5 and a minimum of 21.2. On the same day last year, due to drastic weather changes, there were no maximum or minimum temperatures.

Free Talk

One Can't Talk About Getting Rid of Weeds Without Eliminating Court and Qi.

From Burning Coal Stoves to Education (Part 2)

However, thatch fire has its uses. I learned to burn a coal stove this year. First, put some thatch or paper balls at the bottom of the stove, and cover it with a handful of kindling. Kindling is burned pine charcoal. Next, light the thatch. When the thatch turns to ash, the kindling is burning red. Then, put bituminous coal on top of the kindling. When the kindling turns to ash, the bituminous coal is emitting fierce flames. Finally, cover it with anthracite coal. When the bituminous coal turns to ash, the anthracite coal is already a roaring fire. After that, just keep adding anthracite coal and removing the coal ash, and this stove of roaring fire can burn for a lifetime without being extinguished.

This process of burning coal is like the process of education. Thatch burns kindling, kindling burns bituminous coal, and bituminous coal burns anthracite coal. This order cannot be reversed, or it will be against nature, and labor will be in vain. Relying solely on thatch to start a fire is certainly not possible. Using thatch to directly burn anthracite coal will not work either. Thatch turning to ash cannot ignite anthracite coal. There are three kinds of people in China: one kind uses only thatch to start a fire; one kind likes to pour water on the thatch fire; and one kind uses thatch to quickly burn anthracite coal. Therefore, the life of the Chinese nation has not yet ignited an unquenchable flame, and has not yet emitted sunlight-like brightness.

What is the mission of education? It is not to start a thatch fire, nor to extinguish a thatch fire! It is to ignite the flame of life and emit the light of life according to the process of burning coal. The mission of Chinese education is to ignite the flame of the Chinese nation's life and emit the light of the Chinese nation's life according to the process of burning coal. The mission of world education is also to ignite the flame of all humanity's life and emit the light of all humanity's life according to the process of burning coal.

Wu Luzhen Sells Shunfeng

— Zheng Yimei

Lu Gaojian in front of the Xuanmiao Temple in Suzhou is a well-known cooked meat shop in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. What is called "Shunfeng" is made by chopping the ears of piglets. General Wu Luzhen was not a butcher. How could there be a sale of "Shunfeng"? It turned out that the general once in anger drew his white blade and chopped off the ears of a Japanese slave. At that time, Luzhen was the Border Affairs Minister of Yanji, stern and upright, unparalleled for a time. The Japanese residents in eastern provinces were all terrified by his great name and dared not provoke him in the slightest. One day, when a Japanese consul came to visit, the car was parked outside the gate. Luzhen's commissioner ordered the driver to move it to the side of the road so as not to obstruct traffic. The driver did not know that he was a commissioner, whipped him and insulted him. The commissioner was fluent in Japanese and argued with him. The driver whipped him again, became more aggressive, and added to the insult. The commissioner had no choice but to report to Luzhen. Luzhen was furious and immediately ordered the arrest of the rude driver, grabbed his left ear, and personally used a short blade to chop it off. Blood dripped down, staining his clothes and shoulders red. The driver fell to the ground in pain. The consul questioned him. Luzhen shouted at him, "If you don't know what's good for you and keep babbling, the driver's right ear will also lose its position!" The consul was intimidated and dared not say a word. It became a common story. Luzhen, also known as Shouqing, had revolutionary ideas. During the restoration, Luzhen made many plans, which the Qing court resented. He was assassinated in Shijiazhuang. A generation of heroes was buried in the yellow earth. It is a pity that Luzhen was good at poetry. He composed many poems, such as following Wang Wusheng's original rhyme for keeping watch on New Year's Eve: "The shuttle throws two balls, letting them come and go. White clouds are forever leisurely. All my life I have leaned on rice to float on the vast sea. Ten thousand miles of wind and clouds, I look towards the old mountains. Drunken eyes re-invite the Yan city moon. Hoofprints have spread across the Han dynasty passes. Stroking my thighs, I feel more melancholic. Old traces are endlessly looked up to and down at. What is Wang Lang doing?"

World Tidbits

— Hai Ke

More than 10,000 yuan for a photo. Taking a photo seems like a very ordinary thing. It is not like painting or sculpture, which can get a higher price. Unexpectedly, recently there was a photo that got more than 10,000 silver dollars. This person is a young weaver in Manchester, England, named Charles Powell. He took a photo of his fiancée on a rock on the Isle of Man. It happened to be the opening of a large photography competition. He sent the photo in. Unexpectedly, the result was ranked first in Kodak's worldwide photography competition. He also got a portion of the prize money, one hundred pounds. The national competition prize was one thousand pounds, which is about 10,000 silver dollars, and an extra prize of a silver statue. It is said that this competition received about three million photos from all over the world. A total of forty-seven countries participated. Representatives from eight countries judged the results. The result was that Powell won the top prize. (See page 4 of today's newspaper's pictorial weekly [Cloud and Water Vague] photograph)

"Dare I complain about my fate? My bones have been tempered, my figure is stern. My eyes have seen the rise and fall, many tears of sorrow. A good friend suddenly comes, we play a game of chess. I read old books again, and re-grind my inkstone. I am used to lifting it up for leisurely chanting for five nights. I count the remaining watches and leap at the drum." Also, a rhyming couplet: "Official pavilions, plum blossoms, spring wine are beautiful. Heavenly steps, willows, dawn breeze are sparse." Also, "I still dance when I hear the rooster crowing for five nights. At one time, a butcher of dogs also flew heroically." Also, "Watching chess in Chang'an becomes a broken game. The nations vying for hegemony start a battlefield." Also, "It is not necessary to leave the mountain as a small grass after all. Why refuse to turn the country over to famous flowers." All are works of elegant and lofty talent. Reading them moves people and admires them. The spirit is immortal. Luzhen also has it.

Anecdotes of Feng Yuxiang

— Yan Chonglou

Feng Yuxiang, who has long resided in the countryside, given the urgency of national affairs, took a special train south to discuss plans to save the country with important figures in Beijing and Shanghai. On the day of his arrival in Shanghai, the public saw Feng wearing a short jacket and belt, carrying a cotton cloth coat, with the Gandhi-like demeanor of bringing a spinning wheel and leading a goat. Here are some anecdotes for conversation.

Feng lost his parents at a young age and was extremely poor. He could not support himself. At the end of the late Qing dynasty, each province established a standing army. Literary and military affairs were taught together. Feng joined the army and was valued by his superiors for his hard work and diligence. His position gradually rose because of this. In the Bingyin year, the Yu army invaded Shaanxi. The army defended the city firmly and held out for eight months. The Shaanxi army had no reinforcements, and their food and fodder gradually ran out. We in the city survived on wheat bran and oil residue. Later, even wheat bran and oil residue became precious items. People died one after another in Chang'an. Suddenly, one day, we heard very urgent cannon fire in the distance. The next morning, the siege of the city was lifted. People reported that Feng Yuxiang's army had come and had driven back the Yu army. His use of troops was so rapid. The tens of thousands of soldiers and civilians in the city were revived by Feng's strength.

When Feng was in charge of the Shaanxi government, the silk and satin decoration industries in Qin Province were extremely sluggish. This was because he promoted thrift and set an example by wearing cloth clothes and eating simple meals. Even banquets for guests consisted of no more than one or two dishes of meat. Wu Xintian, the division commander of the Shaanxi army, often said to people, "I would rather gamble and lose two hundred yuan than eat a meal with Feng Yuxiang." This saying became a laughingstock for a time.

A Record of Painting Plums in the Daytime at the Mingqin Studio

— Xiongcun

She Zisheng was skilled in the study of bronze and stone inscriptions. He went to Hunan and obtained a magnetic seal made by Ding Shejingshen, which bore the inscription "Mingqin". He named his studio after it to express his joy. In addition to seal carving, Shengming was also skilled in calligraphy and painting. He and Xiang Zhegong were known as the "Two Talents of Sichuan". Initially, he was quite proud of his iron brush. However, after seeing Zhegong, he sighed that he was a successor to Dun Ding, unparalleled in the world. He abandoned his profession and devoted himself to painting plums, eventually becoming a master of his generation. Zhang Daqian was a famous painter in the country. After seeing Shengming's plum blossoms, he was so beautiful and refined that he admired them with his hands clasped. He once said to people that Zhegong's seal carving was like Dun Ding, and Shengming's plum blossom painting was like Chao Lin. Shengming's plum blossom paintings were marked with Zhegong's seal, making them hard to compare. His admiration for the two was extreme. Shengming traveled to Jiashan and, through Zhegong's introduction, became acquainted with Daqian. All three were born in Sichuan, and all were addicted to painting. They shared the same interests and forgot to sleep while talking. Sometimes, when they were in the mood, Daqian would wield his brush and create ancient pines, twisting and turning. Zhegong would splash ink and paint bamboo, sending his eyes and hands, communicating with the spirit and exhausting the state. Shengming would add plum blossoms to complete the work. Often, more than a dozen sheets would be completed in one night without fatigue.

Looking at Xiang Qi and Talking About [blank]

— Zhu Zumo

After the fall of the Qing dynasty, many of the loyal ministers who went into seclusion regarded the foreign concession as a comfortable nest. Many traces of the old remained in Tianjin and Shanghai in the north and south. They gradually withered away during the twenty years of the Qing dynasty. Recently, Zhu Zumo was heard to have died. The model of the predecessor will not be seen again. Zumo's courtesy name was Guwei, also Ou Yin, and his style name was Jiangcun. His original name was Xiaozang, but he changed it to Zumo to avoid the temple taboo. He was from Wuxing, Zhejiang. In the Guiwei year, he passed the imperial examination with the first place in the second class and was awarded the title of compiler. His calligraphy was modeled after Yan Lugong. During the provincial examination, the son of the Minister of Revenue, Yan Jingming, also imitated Yan's calligraphy. The chief examiner wanted to curry favor with Yan and placed the examination paper at the top. When he opened the seal, he saw that it was Zumo's. Later, he was promoted from attendant bachelor to vice minister of the Ministry of Rites. He asked to return home due to illness while serving as the director of education in Guangdong. He lived in Suzhou and filled in lyrics with Zheng Shuwen (Zhuo) to pass the time. When Emperor Xuantong ascended the throne, he was appointed as an advisor to the Court of Ceremonies but did not take office. During the Boxer Rebellion in the Gengzi year, Empress Dowager Cixi summoned officials to see her and ordered them to speak their minds. Zumo immediately said, "The Empress Dowager shields treacherous parties and relies on rioters to fight against foreign countries. What is her intention? Now that the crisis is imminent, who will she rely on?" The Empress Dowager said, "Dong Fuxiang knows military affairs and is good at fighting. He can be trusted." Fuxiang is昏庸, how can he be relied on?" The Empress Dowager said sternly, "Zumo speaks in a southern accent, and I do not understand him." After he withdrew, the Empress Dowager still glared at him. Everyone thought that he would be severely punished. Later, the Empress Dowager occasionally said to people that although Zumo had spoken out of line, his loyalty was commendable. In recent years, he lived in Shanghai. Lyricists regarded Zumo as the leader of lyrics in the contemporary era and formed the Ou Society, honoring him as the leader. One or two unworthy people were shaken by his reputation and asked to be included in the society. Although Zumo despised their character, he did not refuse them. The generosity and kindness of the elder cannot be matched. Five days before his death, he composed a lyric that was sad and desperate. It was his last work. He died at the age of seventy-five.

Shengming's enthusiasm was particularly high. He often painted several plum blossoms by himself and only stopped when he was satisfied. Pink and black marks were all there. White line drawings and ink halos were all extremely skillful. As the days went by, he created more and more works. From January 9th, he will hold an exhibition at the Jiashan Library for two days. If there are connoisseurs in the world, the style will change. The host of Kan Yun Lou told me that Zhu Guwei, the vice minister, once saw Shengming's ink plum blossoms and said that he could convey his aloof nature. He repeatedly urged him to exhibit his works. Shengming agreed with hesitation. Now that the exhibition is scheduled, the vice minister has suddenly passed away and cannot see it. I am sad. (Transfer rewards to help disaster relief)

Going on Expedition

— A Member of the Youth Support Cavalry

(10) Summary of the Beijing-Shanghai Section (Part 1)

We departed from Shanghai on the morning of the 7th and did not arrive in Nanjing until the afternoon of the 18th. During these eleven days, we traveled through all the major cities on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway. What made us happy and encouraged was that the people everywhere had a determination to save the country. Especially the young students, who would rather endure hunger and cold and call out in all directions. This kind of painstaking effort is truly admirable and praiseworthy. It is only a pity that they waste this precious time.

Since our departure, we have been welcomed and sent off by compatriots everywhere. We have also received comfort, encouragement, flags, expenses, food, and so on. We feel deeply grateful and will wait to kill the enemy and atone for our sins in the future. The two places of Changzhou and Zhenjiang each sent us a broadsword. (Like the ones used by the Feng Army's broadsword team in the past) (Extremely sharp. When you take it out of its scabbard, the cold light shines on people. It can greatly increase the courage of the warriors.

When we marched from Shanghai to Kunshan for several days, the spirit of the entire team was still able to maintain its original state. What was even more commendable was that the female comrades were also very heroic and not tired at all. They still took big steps and bravely advanced. This is truly embarrassing for countless men.

We originally intended to walk to our destination. Later, the railway bureau sincerely advised us, saying that it was feared that it would arouse the patriotic fervor of the people along the way. We also hoped that the national fortune of ["internal peace and external resistance"] would succeed. Therefore, we accepted the kindness of the authorities and took the train from Kunshan onwards.

The Story of Double Buildings Amidst War (5)

— The Happy Master of Seeking Happiness

Chapter 1: An Unparalleled Courtesan Lives Alone, Yearning for Her Beautiful Companion. A Scholar Far From Home, Drifting and Forging a Strange Fate. He used a very sincere tone to bid her farewell, saying, "The dragon is not a thing of the pool. I am an unequal match for you. I don't resent you for betraying me and leaving, but I hope you will behave well in the future and find a happy ending. Don't go back to being a prostitute again, and don't be insecure and be tempted by someone. Don't follow some gigolo and destroy your most precious self. We met in a scene, and I still care about your future." After hearing these words, which were half sarcastic and half admonishing, she calmly replied, "Thank you for treating me so well. If I were not determined to be a good person, I would not be willing to separate from you. Now, please rest assured. I am not that kind of unmindful fool. I had already gotten rid of the evil pimp's bondage when I first married you. From then on, I am a free person again. There are so many things I can do. How can I jump into that fire pit again? As for those sweet-talking and impractical gigolos, I have never looked at them properly. I have this confidence in myself. This kind of person cannot deceive me. I plan to rely on my own strength to make a career in the world and solve my own life. I don't believe that women like us have no ability at all. We don't have to rely on marrying a man to eat and be supported by men. Even if I do choose a promising and capable lover in the future who I can entrust my life to, I will never completely rely on him to live. I won't let him put on the airs of a master to dominate me. I must make him rely on the strength I help and the strategies I preside over to achieve great development and earn a good position. We will coexist and prosper, work together, and he cannot live without me. He cannot disobey me, and I will always tie him to my skirt and hold him in my heart. He will never dare to bully me or betray me." After hearing this proud speech, the old guy stuck out his tongue and replied with a cold smile, as if believing and not believing, "I hope so. Wouldn't that be great? I'm just afraid that such a good man who is willing to obey you will not be easy to find." She then said, "Then I don't necessarily need to marry someone else. I'll do my own thing!" After saying this decisively, they smiled at each other and parted. After that, she rented another beautiful small house and moved all the things from the former small mansion over. She established herself independently. On the outside of the gate was a sign with her own surname. On a strip of red paper, the four big characters "Gusu Liang Residence" were written. Inside, everything for daily life was beautiful and comfortable. But in her heart, she was not satisfied with this. Now that she was full-fledged and could fly at will, she could not suppress her eager ambition. She was going to stride into this free world.

American Cotton Once Rebounded Last Week

But Market Sentiment Became Hesitant Again on the Weekend

A telegram from New York on the 8th reported on the cotton market for the week: At the beginning of last week, the cotton market was slightly sluggish due to short selling, but its supply was bought by colleagues and short covering. After the short selling stopped, it rebounded. The hoarding movement in the South also continued unabated, and the buying interest was also active. The reason is that the securities market situation turned positive, the European financial situation also showed good signs, and the parliament will soon pass economic improvements. However, market sentiment became suspicious again on the weekend, and most people were holding a wait-and-see attitude. The limited supply in the South and the delay of transportation ships due to rain were also reasons. Mr. Carl Wye, a local state government official, said that if cotton farmers realize the seriousness of the situation, they should resolutely implement acreage reduction. At the beginning of December last year, cotton farmers in central Texas convened a conference to request the governor, if satisfactory guarantees could not be obtained in other states, to reduce the cotton acreage to 50% of the lowest limit, then the cotton acreage reduction law should be repealed. However, the governor opposed it, saying that the farmers had sought this from the legislature, and that the cotton-growing states had not yet fallen into this situation.

The only new transaction was Yuanxing's sale of 350 tons of Jiaodang in March, priced at 4 liang, 6 qian, 8 hao, 8 si and a half. Other transactions failed due to disagreement on prices. The return cargo opened 400 to 500 tons, all of which were Xiaotong rice, and the price was slightly weak. Although the arrival and stock of Kexian rice were small, so the outlook should be good, it was difficult to expand due to the impact of foreign arrivals. Yesterday, 100 bags of Taizhou rice were opened, priced at 10 yuan, 0 jiao, 8 jiao, which was also handled by this street. However, the Jiangxi Yuan rice was smoothly handled by the northern gang, and the stock in the market was gradually sold and less and less. The back road was cut off, and the market sentiment and prices were both expected to rise. Yesterday, the northern gang went to Jiangxi to get 500 bags of Kexian Yuan rice, priced at 14 yuan, followed by 13 yuan and a half. The highest prices had already run out of stock.

Flour Suddenly Turned Lively in the Afternoon

Near and Far Each Good Two Eight Plus

Yesterday's flour market: after opening in the morning, the prices of each month showed a sluggish appearance, which was about 5 li lower than the closing price of the previous day. However, because there were very few sellers, the buyers were firm, and it was rapidly proved that most of them had been paid, and their strength seemed to be strong again, so the opening price was gradually stable. Until the opening of the afternoon market, it was still generally flat. Later, due to the deterioration of the Sino-Japanese relations, some nervous people faded away because they heard that the foreign goods were blocked, and small factories bought more. Therefore, the near and far terms suddenly showed a lively trend. As a result, this month was 1 fen and 7 li and a half higher than the previous day, February was 2 fen higher, March was 2 fen and a half higher, April and May were 2 fen and 2 li and a half higher, and June was 2 fen higher.

Wheat Remains Depressed

Yesterday, the market for wheat futures showed a flat and tired appearance in each month. As the end of the year is approaching, the long-term customers of the mainland gangs are gradually closing their positions. Moreover, the delivery of this month has to be brought forward a few days. The factories have foreign goods ready. There is no news of anyone intending to receive the goods in the exchange, so the market sentiment is still depressed, and the distant terms are also falling. As a result, this month fell by 3 fen compared to the previous day, February and March fell by 3 fen, April and May fell by 2 fen, and June was unchanged.

A-Grade French Filature Only Opened at 810 Liang

Yesterday, there was still no turnaround in the foreign silk market in this city. Yesterday, only Da Chang entered 7 packages of Dong filature, and Zhonghe entered 10 packages of Baigan filature, and the price was still flat and tired.

A Glimpse of the Desolate State of Piece Goods, Both Chinese and Foreign

The piece goods market has been in a state of collapse due to the dual pressures of foreign troubles and natural disasters. It has been almost a month since the market came to a halt. Although there has been some activity, it has been minimal. Recently, it has become even quieter. The end of the Western calendar year is approaching, and the general closing period at the end of January is just around the corner. Because of the sealed storage of Eastern goods this year, the industry is feeling difficulties. Therefore, the collapse of goods transactions can be said to be completely immobile. The issue of accounts receivable from other ports is earlier than in previous years, but it is feared that it will be difficult to be satisfied afterwards. The situation of Western goods has been quite stable recently. The inventory of bleached cloth is less than in previous years, and the asking price is quite firm. Taihe's Red Chicken is opened at 13 liang, 2 qian and a half, and the fair Red Little Deer is 12 liang, 8 qian and a half. There has been slight turnover in this street. The Sichuan and Changsha gangs also have an appetite. Poplin, the Changjiang gang, once had some activity, but because the previously ordered goods had been released and arrived, it is feared that it will be difficult to improve, so they have returned to a standstill. Factory yarn woven, foreign yarn plain yarn, etc. are completely immobile. The falling wind of coarse cloth of this factory has stopped. 11-pound are opened at 5 liang, and 9-pound are 4 liang, 7 qian and a half. Bound cloth gradually falls. Balloon is 7 liang, 4 qian, Siping Yun is 7 liang, 3 qian, and Shenxin Chicken is 7 liang, 2 qian, 2 fen and a half. Fashionable goods such as colored striped yarn and plain woven yarn are not plummeting, because the sales route is already limited. Manufacturers are shipping a lot, and the number of dyeing and weaving factories is increasing daily. Because Eastern goods cannot be sold now, and common Western goods are lacking, those in this industry are raising funds to set up factories and produce goods, mostly shoddy serge and straight tribute, in order to make up for the situation.

Hardware Tinplate Sells Smoothly

The tinplate transaction has seen considerable progress recently, such as the acceptance by the cigarette factory gang and the hoarding by the domestic gang, so there have been many transactions. It was found that the number of shipments in the past three days has reached 7,000 to 8,000 boxes. The market, which had been deserted for many days, suddenly presented an optimistic scene. Although the market situation has not risen, it is much better than before. At present, 110-pound thin iron is sold for 38 liang, 200-pound Huisi iron is 25 liang, 5 qian, 90-pound British iron is 10 liang, 100-pound is 13 liang, 90-pound American goods is 14 liang, 100-pound is 16 liang, and 180-pound is 22 liang.

Small Forum

Beware of Conspiracies to Sabotage the Patriotic Movement

Recently, a booklet has been discovered in this city, titled [The True Method of Saving the Nation]. It is said that this booklet is being distributed door-to-door in the dead of night.

The content of the booklet opposes the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association. The so-called true method of saving the nation is to overthrow the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association and reject its inspections. The five methods listed inside are: 1) report to the police and file a public lawsuit; 2) form associations of the same trade and of the same district; 3) petition the court to dissolve the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association; 4) petition the police to ban the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association; 5) petition the government to prohibit the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association. This booklet is not signed and has no publishing location. It is clearly a poisonous hidden arrow and a malicious conspiracy.

I suspect that the distributors of this booklet are Japanese, because the boycott movement is a fatal blow to Japan, and Japan has repeatedly asked our government to ban it. At the same time, I also suspect that those engaged in this dirty business are traitorous merchants in this city, because the boycott movement has indeed caused many disadvantages to the traitorous merchants who rely on selling [Japanese

goods] to get rich. Regardless of whether it is done by the Japanese or by Chinese traitors, there is no doubt that the purpose of this booklet is to sabotage the boycott movement. If it is the Japanese who are engaging in these ghostly tricks, it will only further show their panic and cowardice, which is enough to increase our determination and resolve to boycott Japanese goods. If it is our own people who are engaging in this sabotage of the patriotic movement, then they are truly public enemies of the nation, traitors of the nation, and their crimes are unforgivable.

Our fellow businessmen should recognize that boycotting Japanese goods is our last remaining weapon for resisting violence and saving ourselves, and it is also the most practical and effective method. Before Japan ceases its aggression against us, this weapon must not be relaxed. We should recognize this conspiracy to sabotage the patriotic movement and be careful not to be deceived by this senseless nonsense that has lost its spirit. Only with a nation can there be a home; saving the home starts with saving the nation. Boycotting Japanese goods saves the nation, while selling Japanese goods at most only allows one's own family to earn some profit. Everyone should carefully recognize the importance of the matter.

Popular Science

First Aid for Electric Shock Pillar Middle

Once someone is shocked by electricity, is sucked by the electric wire and cannot break free, immediately notify the power plant to cut off the current. Before the current is cut off, never try to rescue! But if you know that the current; is direct current, voltage below 500 volts (commonly known as pounds) or alternating current 'voltage below 300 volts, you can very carefully rescue like this... Use a very dry wooden pole five or six feet long (the longer the better) and a very dry rope two fathoms long, pull the shocked person off the electric wire. If the electric wire sucks the shocked person too tightly, you can only cut the electric wire with an axe, but the handle of this axe must be very dry wood and more than five feet long, and you must wrap your hands well with very thick, dry cloth (preferably wool or silk)! Cut off the wires on both sides of the shocked person at the same time!

After rescuing the shocked person, if he already appears dead, do not think that he cannot be saved! Immediately send him to a place with ventilation, and try to restore his breathing. Pull his tongue once, or use other artificial respiration methods; at the same time, restore his blood circulation, pat his torso with your palms or a hot towel, sprinkle cold water on his face one after another, and finally make him smell ammonia water, and he can be revived.

Within the possible range, it is always advisable to call a doctor as soon as possible.

Street Sociology

Alley Snapshot Phoenix Dance

The Sister-in-law in the Garret

People who have not lived in Shanghai' seem not to feel the wonderfulness of [titles]. Common titles for men are mostly Mr. Common titles for women are mostly Mrs., Grandma, Miss, or Good Woman, Sister-in-law. These titles are generally about the same everywhere. What about Shanghai? The titles for women must be given a special title. Clothing, food, housing, and transportation are the four major elements of life. And among the four elements, in Shanghai, the word [housing] is the most difficult. It goes without saying for the class of people who sit in cars and live in foreign houses: an ordinary building often houses four or five families. Garret family, main hall family, side building family. Then the problem of titles arises. If you call someone "Sister-in-law," people will definitely not understand who you're referring to… Sister-in-law upstairs in the main hall? Or Sister-in-law in the garret?

In this way, in addition to the common "Sister-in-law," "Good Woman," and "Grandma," special nouns must be prefixed. So there are "Sister-in-law in the garret," "Good Woman upstairs in the main hall," "Grandma in the side building," "Elder Sister in the room next door…" titles.

If ladies, grandmas, and misses who sit in cars and live in foreign houses hear these titles, they must say, "Ah! How strange!"

Southeast Northwest

Vegetarian and Meat Dishes

K Jun created the idea, Dirt Buddha Runwen

Psychological Vegetarian—Psychological Meat

Fish, meat, shrimp, crab… are meat dishes. Vegetables, greens, melons, beans… are vegetarian dishes. Everyone knows this.

But in ancient monasteries, there were eminent monks and virtuous elders who, though nominally monks, actually ate meat. As far as I know, there are many such cases. Probably these eminent monks have a thorough understanding of the principles of Taoism: the mind is the Buddha, so what harm is there in eating meat? Form is emptiness, so why bother with vegetarianism? The ancients said, [There is a prostitute in the eye, but no prostitute in the heart,] that is what these people are like. Someone gave Master Dexin forty chicken eggs, and the Master swallowed them all. Many people laughed at him, and the Master composed a verse:

[A mouthful contains the chaotic universe, there is neither skin nor blood nor hair. This old monk will take you to the Western Paradise, so you can avoid being

killed in the world.]

They have their own explanations for eating meat. I can't do anything with these people, I call them psychological vegetarians. There are already quite a few vegetarian restaurants open in Shanghai, and their business is also very prosperous. But what I don't understand is, since it is a vegetarian restaurant, it is naturally completely vegetarian. Excellent turnips should be fried as turnips, and braised tofu should be braised as tofu, but they insist on adding the names of meat dishes, such as

vegetarian chicken, vegetarian duck, vegetarian fish, vegetarian meat... Why bother?

Probably a few old adventurers who opened restaurants are good at guessing the psychology of society. Because now there are a few gentlemen who eat vegetarian food, but they are not sincerely eating vegetarian food, but are eating vegetarian food as a fad. I also eat vegetarian food, but eating vegetarian food is not comfortable or enjoyable. So the old adventurers who opened vegetarian restaurants use a method of [quenching thirst with plums] [satisfying hunger with painted cakes], making the name meaty but the substance vegetarian. Sure enough! It is greatly welcomed by the general public of vegetarian eaters! I call these people psychological carnivores. I have a friend who also used to eat vegetarian food, but he doesn't eat meat, but he eats the by-products cooked in meat. He doesn't eat fish, but he eats the by-products cooked in fish. The same goes for chicken, duck, and other things. This is another innovation in eating vegetarian food. I once laughed at him and said, [You

are truly a

dropout among meat eaters,

a revolutionary among vegetarians,

you can be regarded as a bat in the eating world!]

Special Translation of the Christmas of the White Russians in This City

The calendar used by the Orthodox Church is about two weeks different from the calendar used by the Catholic Church and the Protestant Church. The seventh day is the Orthodox Christmas, which is a big festival for the Slavs. The White Russians in this city all have banquets and celebrations.

On the eve of Christmas, Russian men and women go to church to pray and perform the Mass. After that, they hold lit candles and return home at dawn. This scene could still be seen in the French Concession yesterday morning.

Russian families also set up Christmas trees, and children often boast about their rich decorations to their peers. On Christmas Day, groups of children receive sweets from Santa Claus under the tree. Also, on Christmas Eve, when friends gather and a large banquet is opened, a bundle of dry grass is often placed under the tablecloth, so that guests do not forget the items in the cradle where Jesus was born.

Their recipes are also very special, with only fish, vegetables, and mutton stew. Although there is a plate of rich roast goose next to it, guests who have a gluttonous taste, even if they are drooling, can only look at it and dare not taste it. Slavs regard this as a delicacy for tomorrow and are not allowed to eat it. In addition, on the morning of Christmas, children go to relatives to congratulate them, and there is also a custom of receiving sweets and money, which is similar to the old custom of pressing down the year in our country. Shanghai Story

Shanghai Story (3)

The First Cannon Outside Wusongkou

In his report [The Voyage of the Amherst to the Northern Ports of China], Lindeus highly praised Shanghai as an excellent commercial entry point, but the East India Company dismissed it. At that time, the British decided to use the Zhoushan Islands as the center of British trade with China. The importance of Shanghai had not yet been felt.

Since the Opium War began in the twentieth year of Daoguang, the first cannon outside Wusongkou awakened the sleeping land, and Shanghai's new fate began to descend. Whether this new fate is a blessing or a curse, we cannot determine now. But just for Shanghai, the unprecedented sound of British warships broke its poor and unbearable fate and embarked on a new path of prosperity and wealth, which is not Shanghai's blessing. But [fortune never comes twice, misfortune never comes alone]. Since then, Shanghai has become a blessed den of demons in the Far East.

In the twenty-second year of Daoguang (1842 AD), British generals William Parker and Bird Gu led an army of 4,000 men, attacked and captured Xiamen, Ningbo, and Zhapu successively, and arrived directly at Wusongkou on June 13.

A Bloody Battle

The Shanghai officials had no prior preparations for coastal defense. Once they discovered that the British army was about to attack Shanghai, they made every effort to defend themselves in a hurry, repaired the forts on both sides of Wusongkou, and built earthen embankments along the Yangtze River, from Wusong to Baoshan County, a length of three English miles. They collected earthen cannons, bird guns, and short guns to prepare for battle.

In addition to the garrison soldiers, they also temporarily recruited village braves. At that time, there were 3,000 soldiers from Xuzhou, Henan, and Jiangning, and 800 rattan shield soldiers, but they had not been trained for a long time and their military equipment was not sufficient. The weakness of the military force is self-evident. The most interesting thing was the invention of waterwheels tied to both sides of sand boats, using human power to move the wheels and stir the waves, which could travel three English miles per hour.

The British fleet proceeded very slowly due to unfamiliar waterways. On the dawn of June 16, the British used steamships to tow warships forward, approaching our army, only about 500 yards apart. At this time, our army fired all cannons, piercing three British warships, killing three people and injuring several others. In the end, due to the imprecision of the weapons, our country was defeated. The British soldiers then landed and went straight to Baoshan. Our army retreated to Suzhou. In this bloody battle, the military and civilians of Shanghai and the officials bravely resisted. As a result, more than 200 people died and countless were injured.

The Fall of Shanghai

British warships sailed into the Suzhou River and arrived at Xinzha Bridge. The army landed and occupied the county seat. There were very few soldiers in the city. After a little resistance, they immediately withdrew. The order in the city was in chaos, and the people fled the city one after another. The gangsters took the opportunity to rob and loot. The British army also searched and plundered, leaving nine out of ten houses empty, which was the first great robbery in Shanghai in nearly a hundred years.

After the British army occupied Shanghai, they sent people to measure the water volume in the upper reaches of the Huangpu River. British General Parker and others also went to Songjiang to observe the situation. A week later, the British warships left Shanghai and sailed to Nanjing on June 23.
